Soliciting Information on Health and Medicine Conditions from Various Regions 185

Since its founding, this publication has been running for nearly two years, and it has consistently taken the initiation and promotion of new medicine and the advancement of national health as its mission. However, due to the limited talent and knowledge of our colleagues, we are concerned about potential oversights. We now specifically welcome both official reports and private investigations. We require accurate materials and detailed reports. Once received, they will be published immediately, and a small fee will be provided to express our gratitude. Sincerely, The Shen Bao Medical Weekly Society.

The Importance of Tuberculosis Among School Children in Shanghai City (Part 1) 186

— Li Ting'an

Tuberculosis among school children in Shanghai City is relevant not only to students in school but also to children at home. This can be discussed in three points. Before discussing these points, let us first introduce:

What is Tuberculosis?

Tuberculosis is caused by infection with the tuberculosis bacillus. If we have tuberculosis and the sputum we cough up undergoes a specific procedure, many red rod-shaped bacteria can be detected. These bacteria are called tuberculosis bacilli. When they invade our lungs, they can eat away at our lungs and damage blood vessels, causing bleeding. Mild cases may go unnoticed, with the patient appearing normal. Later, as the ulcers grow larger and toxins spread, the face becomes pale and thin, weight decreases, and fever often occurs in the afternoon with an elevated body temperature. Normal body temperature is 37 degrees Celsius, while tuberculosis patients often have temperatures ranging from 37.5 to 38 degrees Celsius. Children at this stage are prone to anger. Further ulceration leads to coughing, but not frequently, only one or two coughs at a time. In severe cases, there is bleeding, emaciation, and cold sweats (sweating without being hot). At this point, the lung ulcers are larger, and the patient becomes a mere skeleton, a "tuberculosis ghost!" This is the third stage of tuberculosis and is very difficult to cure. Upon examination by a doctor, highly abnormal localized symptoms are found in the lungs, and X-rays can reveal the damaged areas. Bacterial examination will reveal tuberculosis bacilli. Tuberculosis is easily treated in its early stages. The first stage is still treatable, but by the third stage, there is little that can be done. Tuberculosis bacilli entering the intestines cause intestinal tuberculosis, and entering the skin causes skin tuberculosis. They can grow anywhere, but the lungs are their favorite place to reside.

The symptoms of tuberculosis usually include the aforementioned fever, cough, and cold sweats; however, some cases involve direct bleeding without going through these processes, which are atypical symptoms. In our country, 400 out of every 100,000 people die from tuberculosis each year. With a population of 400 million, a simple calculation shows that a total of 1.6 million "tuberculosis ghosts" are produced each year! The Japanese massacre of our compatriots during the Battle of Shanghai was temporary, but deaths from tuberculosis occur every year, making this issue worthy of study. A century ago, the United Kingdom was like our country, with 400 out of every 100,000 people dying from tuberculosis each year. Now, only 80 people die each year, a reduction to one-fifth. This indicates the development of public health and a decrease in infectious diseases. This is the first point I want to discuss with everyone.

The Status of Tuberculosis Among School Children in Shanghai City

Now, let's talk about the topic at hand, the status of tuberculosis among school children in Shanghai City. Last year, the China Anti-Tuberculosis Association was established in Shanghai to promote anti-tuberculosis work because we learned that this issue is very important and that victory over "tuberculosis ghosts" is very achievable. Based on past experience, various countries have won battles, and our country should be no exception. Therefore, the Bureau of Health and the Bureau of Education cooperated to conduct a tuberculosis screening test called the "Tuberculin Test." The test method involves drying the bacteria, grinding them into powder, mixing them with saline, placing the mixture in a glass bottle, drawing a small amount with a syringe, and injecting it under the skin, causing a blister to form. After several hours, those without tuberculosis show no reaction, while those with tuberculosis show significant redness in the area. This is a method to test whether we have tuberculosis. Last autumn, the Bureau of Health specifically invited Dr. Gao Jinglang to conduct tuberculosis screenings at the Municipal Bide School. A total of 822 students were tested, of whom 542 had a positive reaction, proving that more than 60% had tuberculosis. Therefore, the parents of these 542 students were advised to have X-rays taken at the Red Cross Hospital at a reduced cost. In total, 129 agreed to be examined, and the results sent to the hospital for treatment showed that 33 were severe, 57 were mild, and 34 were very mild. If all 542 people had been examined, there would have been 15 very severe cases and 100 severe cases. From this, we discovered several issues worthy of research:

1. The patients themselves, those with severe illnesses, continue to attend school, which will likely lead to death in the future. Therefore, teachers should focus on nurturing rather than solely on teaching. In the past, emphasis was placed on teaching rather than nurturing, neglecting the students' health, which had a significant impact on their well-being. This is in stark contrast to Director Pan's idea of integrating education and nurturing. Gentlemen, you have spent a lot of energy teaching a class of students, but unfortunately, they die, which is very unworthy. Therefore, I hope we can implement Director Pan's principle of combining teaching and nurturing. What has been said above is based on the statistical finding that the first harm of tuberculosis is to the physical health and academic progress of school children. (To be continued)

Overview of Medical and Health Conditions in Anqing (Part 2)

— Jiang Huiming

(4) Group Activities and Academic Research of New and Old Medicine

The members of the new medicine community have mostly received higher education from the state. Naturally, they have a clear understanding of groups. The new medicine community in Anqing has organized the Huaining County Medical Association, with approximately 50 members. Those in charge of the association are able to work together sincerely, and the external influence is still very strong.

In the early years of the Republic of China, the old medicine community had already established the "Chinese Medicine Association." Although the name of an academic organization was used, it still involved the work of a professional association. In 1930, the tide of medical revolution promoted by new medicine was surging, and the nationwide call for changing the name of Chinese medicine to national medicine was deafening. During that period, the Chinese Medicine Association in Anqing was brewing to change its name to the "National Medicine Association." Due to the lack of understanding of groups among the old medicine members, it was not until this spring that it slowly and painfully emerged. The total number of members is about one hundred or so. However, the organization is loose, the work is lax, the opinions are complex, and the funding is insufficient, showing no vitality at all. Although there are a few enthusiastic people who are actively carrying out everything, as the saying goes, "One tree cannot support a tall building," they are also powerless.

In the early years of the Republic of China, Anqing had established an official medical bureau, which was managed by old medicine practitioners. After the success of the National Revolution, the Anhui provincial government established a relief hospital and changed the name of the old official medical bureau to a medical service center, which was subordinate to the relief hospital. At this time, the content of the medical service center was different from before, and the medical services were shared by new and old medicine practitioners.

Speaking of academic organizations, there are very few in Anqing. In 1932, the author and well-known local medical professionals such as Mr. Yin Zizheng organized an "Oriental Medical Research Association" and successively published "Medical Innovation" and "Medical Weekly" in the Anqing "Republic of China Daily" and "Xin Wan Duo Bao," which were able to arouse the attention of the society. During that time, the Huaining County Medical Association once took charge of the "Medical Special Issue" and the Jiansheng Hospital published the "Jiansheng Medical Report." Unfortunately, they were all limited by personnel changes and insufficient financial resources, and eventually disappeared like a flash in the pan. Even now, thinking back, there is still lingering pain!

Attached is a list of medical and pharmaceutical publications:

Jiansheng Medical Report

Editors: Wu Jiansheng, et al.

Publisher: Jiansheng Hospital

Medical Bi-Weekly

Editor: Oriental Medical Research Association

Publisher: Anhui Republic of China Daily

Editors: Zhang Yao, Yin Zizheng, Jiang Huiming, et al.

Publisher: Anqing Xin Wan Duo Bao Daily

Publisher: Anqing Wan Bao Newspaper

(5) Investigation of Anqing Hospitals and Author's Opinions

The development of new medicine in Anqing to what it is today is largely due to the hard work and struggle of the new medicine comrades in Anqing. It is indeed not easy. The atmosphere in Anqing in the early years of the Republic of China was quite conservative. When new medicine practitioners gave injections to patients, those patients would be genuinely frightened and run away. Of course, there are no such jokes now. However, the shortage of doctors and the uneven level of doctors in such an environment do not allow us to be too demanding. However, there is something that the author cannot condone from my new medicine comrades in Anqing, and that is that there are too many hospitals in Anqing that do not live up to their names. Especially in recent years, in the process of the vigorous development of new medicine in Anqing, the rise of hospitals is also like bamboo shoots after a rain. Those who can establish clinics in a down-to-earth manner are only the Cheng Liming Clinic and the Xinglin Treatment Center. Is this a good phenomenon after all? Looking at the hospital management regulations promulgated by the state, there are too many places that do not conform. New medicine comrades who aspire to and love new medicine, please pay attention to the true value of being legitimate and well-founded. Do not ignore the overall problem of new medicine and society in the future.

I believe that it is more appropriate for our new medicine practitioners to establish specialized clinics in Anqing in the future. Because Anqing lacks specialist doctors. We want to improve patients' belief in new medicine and break the stereotype that new medicine is good at surgery and old medicine is good at internal medicine. Only specialized technology can show the essence and value of science.

(6) Business Conditions of New and Old Pharmaceutical Industries

Before 1931, the old pharmaceutical industry was quite prosperous. Because Anqing had not suffered any major devastation since the floods of 1901, including the various recoveries and the Northern Expedition. All businesses were able to flourish, and the old pharmaceutical industry was no exception. In 1931, the great flood in the Yangtze River flooded the farmland in various counties along the Yangtze River in Anhui, causing the rural areas to go bankrupt and the business to be depressed. Also, due to the increasingly tight financial situation in the inland, the old pharmaceutical industry was also greatly affected. Generally, the largest wholesale pharmacies had difficulty collecting accounts from rural towns. For retail pharmacies, the most profitable were ginseng, bird's nest, and ointment pills. Generally, middle-class families practiced thrift and did not prescribe tonics, so the business income was also greatly reduced. According to statistics, there are about seventy to eighty old pharmacies of various sizes in the city, but the size of the business also varies greatly. The largest pharmacies can reach an annual business volume of forty to fifty thousand yuan.

On the surface, the new pharmaceutical industry seems to be thriving, but in reality, it is also suffering from the setbacks of natural disasters, resulting in a strong exterior but a weak interior. There are indeed very few with real strength. There are only fourteen new pharmacies in the city. Besides selling some over-the-counter drugs, medical devices, and all kinds of cosmetics, only Huayang and Pu Bo Li pharmacies can fill prescriptions for doctors. However, there has not been a formally licensed pharmacist in charge of filling prescriptions, which is indeed a regret for the new medical and pharmaceutical community in Anqing. As for the business volume of large pharmacies, each can reach more than ten thousand yuan.

The business competition between the new and old pharmaceutical industries is not tense in Anqing. The old pharmaceutical industry established the "Pharmaceutical Industry Association" very early. In recent years, the new pharmaceutical industry has also organized the "Pharmaceutical Industry Association." In terms of spirit, the new Pharmaceutical Industry Association is more energetic; in terms of funding, the old Pharmaceutical Industry Association is more sufficient. There was once a rumor that the new and old pharmaceutical groups were merging, but this has not yet been realized.

(7) Conclusion

What is written above is just a microcosm of the medical and health situation in Anqing. It is certainly not enough to be regarded as documentary material. When the author concludes this article, in addition to hoping that people from all over the world who are concerned about medicine and health will provide more such materials for reference, I also hope that enthusiastic people in medicine and health can formulate a form that lists the points that need to be understood, divides them into categories, and distributes them to local medical associations or health agencies or private individuals to fill in. I think the future gains will be more orderly and meet the needs of the standard. Medical and health experts who sympathize with our requirements, please work together!

Common Knowledge Questions and Answers on Diseases 187

— Cheng Hanzhang

(4)(10)(1) Gastroptosis and Gastric Atony

(Question) What is gastroptosis?

(Answer) It is a disease in which the position of the stomach is lower than its normal position.

(Question) How can gastroptosis occur?

(Answer) People with weak constitutions, women who wear tight corsets, those whose upper abdomen is compressed, those with reduced abdominal pressure, women after childbirth, or patients with ascites after puncture, pendulous abdomen, excessive fat, and people with weak abdominal muscles are all prone to gastroptosis.

(Question) What are the symptoms after gastroptosis occurs?

(Answer) No matter how obvious the degree of prolapse, it does not cause any particular obstacles. However, patients feel pressure, fullness, belching, vomiting, and stomach pain. It is also accompanied by gastric motility disorders or secretion disorders.

(Question) What can be seen on the outside of the abdomen?

(Answer) The patient's upper abdomen is sunken, while the area below the navel is very bulging.

(Question) What are the abnormalities during palpation?

(Answer) When the bulging abdomen is suddenly touched with a finger, a clear fluctuating sound can be heard.

(Question) What other diseases can be complicated?

(Answer) It is mostly complicated by gastric atony and gastrectasis. It can also be complicated by gastroptosis and enteroptosis.

(Question) What medicines should be taken and how should attention be paid to diet when treating gastroptosis?

(Answer) The patient's physique should be strengthened first, and tonics such as arsenic preparations and quinine preparations can be taken internally. For diet, nutritious and small portions should be selected, and each time, one should not eat or drink as much as possible to reduce the burden on the stomach.

(Question) Are there any physical therapy methods to treat this gastroptosis?

(Answer) Yes. Like applying an abdominal belt to elevate the stomach; or using electrotherapy, massage, and hydrotherapy to make the abdominal muscles and stomach muscles tense and strong; all can be tried.

(Question) Can it be treated with surgery?

(Answer) There is a gastropexy in surgery, which may be performed.

(Question) What is gastric atony?

(Answer) A symptom of flaccid and weak muscles in the stomach wall.

(Question) How does this gastric atony occur?

(Answer) Some are congenital, some are caused by overeating, which leads to overwork or flaccidity of the stomach muscles, and some are caused by repeated childbirths.

(Question) What are the symptoms of gastric atony?

(Answer) Patients often experience food stagnation, fermentation, and decay. There are fluctuating sounds in the stomach, and there are also symptoms of autointoxication, such as headache, heaviness, neurological discomfort, measles, slow or excited heart rate, terror, chest tightness, and dizziness. Severe gastric atony is easily complicated by gastrectasis. Or it may be combined with gastroptosis.

(Question) How should the treatment method for gastric atony be?

(Answer) It can be treated according to the method for gastroptosis. If putrefaction and fermentation occur in the stomach, or if autointoxication occurs, gastric lavage should be performed, and antiseptic and disinfectant agents such as Resoroin and Salo () should be taken internally.

Common Treatment Methods for Fever (Part 2) 188

— Li Xing

If the fever is not too high, there is no need to take antipyretic drugs or use other methods to reduce the fever. If the fever is too high, appropriate methods can be used to reduce the fever to avoid extreme damage to the body. A low-grade fever is beneficial to the disease. The most common febrile diseases are tuberculosis, typhoid fever, heart inflammation, pneumonia, empyema, throat inflammation, appendicitis, or any part of the body with pus or sores. Pus-producing diseases, appendicitis, etc., on the one hand, need surgical resection, and on the other hand, they also need common treatment methods. Common treatment methods are like a country defending against foreign insults, which must first strengthen its national power. In addition to specific symptomatic treatment, common treatment methods are suitable for any fever. In particular, pulmonary tuberculosis, typhoid fever, pneumonia, and heart inflammation require extra attention to common treatment methods. Whether or not common treatment is used has a great relationship with whether these diseases turn from death to life. And if the patient understands this medical theory, the common treatment method can be done by himself. The common treatment methods are described below:

(1) Quiet Rest

Even if the fever is not too high, you must rest quietly, because there is a kind of war in the body. It is certainly not easy to know how intense the war will be in the future. The body is like a country that must prepare for a long-term war when it encounters an invader. A strong national power and sufficient preparation can lead to final victory. Is the body not the same? If the body's initial killing power against invading bacteria is very fierce, but it completely loses its resistance in the end, even a very minor problem can lead to death. We often see patients whose condition is very mild, but because they have no resistance, they often die. Therefore, at the beginning of the disease, rest quietly to cultivate the body's ability to resist bacteria and allow all the cells of the body to fully participate in the battle. If the resistance is sufficient, even a serious illness can be easily revived.

Someone asked, what does quiet rest actually mean? Quiet rest means this: people with fever should rest in bed day and night 丨丨Not just resting in bed, there should be comprehensive nursing. The bed should feel comfortable, not moving too much, and bowel movements should be done in bed. The bedroom must have fresh air, and do not [be afraid of being blown by the wind]. It must be known that fresh air is of great benefit to people without illness. Isn’t it even more important to people who are sick? As long as there is no strong wind blowing directly, it will not harm the patient. Fresh air will not harm people. Once I was invited to see a doctor, and when I arrived at a house, a woman had a normal postpartum fever. No one in the family took care of her, only a maid served her. The woman started to have a fever in the morning, and the doors and windows of the front building where she lived were tightly closed (the weather was still hot in autumn). The patient's fever gradually increased until she became comatose. Her maid then told the neighbors. The neighbors then volunteered to ask me to come. When I arrived in the house, I felt stuffy and hot, and the patient's temperature was 107 degrees. Later, her obstetrician arrived, and I left. Later, I heard that the woman died that night. If there was fresh air in the room, the temperature would not have risen to 107 degrees so suddenly. This is just one example. I think many people know a common chemical experiment. That is, covering a burning candle with a large glass bottle, and the candle flame will immediately become smaller and go out. People without illness need fresh air to survive, so do people with serious illnesses need fresh air ten or a hundred times more?

When the patient is resting quietly, someone also needs to take care of him so that he does not catch cold after sweating. Wet clothes must be carefully changed. The patient also needs to wash his body once or twice a day. For the body washing method, use a towel with warm water to wash the patient part by part with soap, and then wipe it dry with a dry towel. Clean skin can help the body excrete waste. In addition to washing the body, rubbing the back with alcohol every night can prevent bedsores from developing on the back after lying down for a long time. Help the patient turn over several times a day to prevent pneumonia from developing in the lower part of the lungs (especially important for the elderly). The bed sheets on which the patient lies should always be flattened, and there should not be a single wrinkle.

Quiet rest is not only for the body to rest, but also for the mind to rest. Patients should put all thoughts of self-interest aside.

. If the fever is not high and you are resting in bed for a long time, some beneficial hobbies are also okay. Especially those who are resting for a long time due to pulmonary tuberculosis or heart disease, it is also good to spend some time learning natural science, foreign languages, shorthand, basket weaving, or hand weaving during the day. As for games that involve competition, they are harmful to the body and should not be done, because they can easily make the patient too tired.

People with fever must have adequate sleep. Adequate sleep has a great relationship with the future recovery. If the patient does not get enough sleep at night, he can be asked to sleep during the day. If the patient's environment is particularly quiet, it is probably not difficult to sleep. When recuperating at home, you must pay attention to the patient's environment and ensure that it is quiet. If there is really no way to sleep, you can take a small amount of sleeping pills. If the fever is too high and the patient is unconscious, one or two people must always be by the bedside to prevent the patient from falling off the bed or other unfortunate accidents from happening. (To be continued)

A Brief Introduction to Pulmonary Tuberculosis (24) 189

— Hu Jiayan

Chapter 8 Clinical Examination Methods

If someone has already found some, or even all, of the various symptoms described in the previous chapter, then is there no doubt that this person has pulmonary tuberculosis? Of course, it won't be that simple. We must know that the general symptoms of this disease, such as weight loss, poor appetite, and pale complexion, this kind of latent process, can be imagined or speculated, but it is not inevitable. Measuring the daily temperature is considered the most reliable; but for a type that starts acutely, it is still indistinguishable from a common cold, and other symptoms can be deduced from this. If we want to solve this major doubt, (whether it is pulmonary tuberculosis without a doubt?) that is, in addition to the subjective symptoms described by the patient, the doctor should also re-evaluate and try to prove it from an objective perspective; the various details in this are the clinical examination methods described in this chapter! Taking a step back, even if the disease has been correctly diagnosed based on a few symptoms, this procedure cannot be omitted. Readers, please remember that it was mentioned in the fifth chapter that this disease has several classifications due to different pathological and anatomical properties; the prognosis in this regard is different, and the treatment is also different. For example, metal preparations and tuberculin for this disease are very suitable for chronic proliferative types, but they are not suitable if it is an exudative acute start. The success of artificial pneumothorax in treating this disease is well-known; but for this disease with too wide an area of infiltration and too many cavities, it is still necessary to think twice before acting. This kind of judgment of whether or not can not be done based on the subjective symptoms described by the patient; clinical examination methods such as percussion, auscultation, and X-ray examination can not be omitted at this time. This kind of work, on the surface, looks very trivial, but it is actually discerning and worthy of [seeing the essence through the appearance] without shame.

Common Sense on Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Hygiene 190

— Tang Renjin

(18) Trachoma

If trachoma reaches a significant degree and is not treated, various dangerous symptoms and complications will arise. I will now briefly discuss them separately, as follows:

(1) Trachomatous Pannus: This is the most common and easily occurring primary sign in trachoma. Its cause is due to the excessive depth of trachoma. The surface of the cornea (commonly known as the "eye black") gradually becomes cloudy. The epithelium of the cornea also proliferates simultaneously. On the other hand, new blood vessels form, so the appearance of pannus is a fleshy, grayish-white color with blood streaks. Its location begins at the upper edge of the cornea and gradually progresses downward. Once it encroaches upon the pupillary area, the patient will immediately experience vision impairment. If the entire cornea is affected, it is equivalent to blindness.

(2) Corneal Ulcer: Often occurs on the edge of the cornea or concurrently with pannus. It develops at the junction with healthy cornea. After this type of ulcer heals, it often leaves behind opacity, impairing vision.

(3) Eyelid Curvature and Ingrown Eyelashes: If trachoma is not treated properly in its mild stages, the conjunctiva and cartilage may contract due to scarring in the future, causing the eyelid to curve. At this time, eyelashes often grow inward, irritating the cornea and causing inflammation. Or, on the upper eyelid, entropion (inward turning of the eyelid) may occur; on the lower eyelid, ectropion (outward turning of the eyelid) may occur.

(4) Keratoconjunctivitis Sicca (Dry Eye): Because of conjunctival atrophy, its secretory function disappears, and tear production gradually decreases. Its viscosity also increases. At this time, the patient's eyes feel dry, and the surface of the cornea becomes thickened, dry, and opaque. If patients with trachoma develop this dry eye condition, it is very difficult to cure. Even if the patient has already become blind, this feeling of dryness is still unavoidable.

(5) Corneal Nebula: When pannus gradually absorbs and returns to transparency, corneal nebula often remains.

(6) Ptosis (Drooping Upper Eyelid): We often see that the upper eyelids of patients with trachoma often droop. Their eyes seem to be closed all day long.

Whether the prognosis of trachoma is good or bad is a difficult question to answer. It depends entirely on the severity of trachoma, the timing of treatment, whether the treatment is appropriate, and the patient's patience, etc. Therefore, sometimes it can be completely cured, sometimes it leaves behind vision impairment or complications, and sometimes dangerous symptoms gradually worsen and lead to blindness.

The prevention of trachoma can be divided into two types: broad and narrow. The narrow sense of prevention is that individuals pay attention to eye hygiene, such as (1) not using public towels and washbasins; (2) not getting too close to relatives and friends who have trachoma. Direct or indirect transmission of trachoma must be avoided. As for the broad sense of prevention, its scope is even wider. It is (1) the government must take the lead in promoting [how to eradicate this shameful national disease]; (2) social leaders are responsible for implementing publicity work, with the same spirit as handling the prevention and treatment of cholera in the summer; (3) school authorities must supervise school doctors to examine students for trachoma. If there is mild trachoma, they should be instructed to receive treatment. If it is severe, they should be temporarily suspended from school and sent home to seek medical treatment, so as to avoid transmission among classmates. We know that students are important building blocks of the country and also the future representatives of the country. If they are all infected with trachoma, wouldn't they become trachoma building blocks and the future trachomatous representatives of the country? This is a very painful and shameful thing. Therefore, I want to advise school authorities to pay more attention to the prevention of trachoma. Speaking of which, it may be more important than guiding education. (4) Responsible personnel in prisons and factories should also implement trachoma prevention, because people are crowded and it is easier to spread the disease.

Speaking of the treatment of trachoma, it can generally be divided into two types: drug treatment and surgical treatment. Its main purposes are (1) to minimize damage to the conjunctiva; (2) to minimize damage to physiological functions; (3) to prevent scarring; (4) to avoid corneal complications; and (5) to reduce inflammation and its secretions. Regarding drug treatment, it is not necessarily to be treated by an ophthalmologist. Most regular doctors can treat it. If drug treatment cannot achieve the desired cure, then surgical treatment should be performed by an ophthalmologist. The most suitable time for surgery is when the inflammation has subsided, secretions have decreased, conjunctival congestion and opacity have subsided, and granules have appeared in a limited area, etc. The purpose of surgery is to fundamentally remove the pathological products of trachoma and to preserve the physiological function of the conjunctiva. Its methods include cauterization, expression, crushing, pressing, and wiping, etc. Regarding the question of which method is better, it must of course be determined by a doctor after examining the condition.

(Corrigendum) In the previous issue, the "驗" (yàn - examination) in "眼臉之驗" (examination of the eyelids) was misprinted as "臉" (liǎn - face), and the "所" (suǒ - that which) in "所以在臨床上觀察砂眼起來之所" (that which is observed clinically in the development of trachoma) was misprinted as "可" (kě - can).

Introduction to [New Book on Childhood Infectious Diseases] 191

— Yan Siru

Mr. Gao Naolang, director of the pediatrics department of the Red Cross Hospital, has recently written a book entitled [Childhood Infectious Diseases]. The content is very rich. According to the editor, the motivation for writing this book has been long in the making. Initially, he planned to choose a good foreign pediatric textbook and translate several thousand words a day, estimating that it would be completed in about a year. However, after careful examination of various European and American pediatric textbooks, none were satisfactory. If he were to arbitrarily modify them during translation, it would lack credibility. This is because foreign pediatric textbooks generally have two characteristics: first, they each seek to apply to the specific conditions of their own country; and second, the authors specialize in certain diseases, and their descriptions of those conditions are particularly detailed. This is certainly the highlight of each book, but when transferred to our country, it immediately loses its luster. Our country is vast and populous, and the climate and geography are vastly different in the north and south. Customs and habits also vary in the east and west. The types of diseases and their distribution, the course of the disease, and the prognosis all differ within the country. Compared to foreign countries, the differences are even more numerous. Therefore, he changed his approach and decided to compile his own book in order to make it applicable.

The editor also said that from a historical perspective, although the progress of our country's scientific medicine should be faster, it has already made great strides compared to thirty years ago. Moreover, there are quite a few clinicians in various places who are devoted to research. If he were to compile his own book, this most valuable local material could be adopted. The difficulty is that there is no systematic index of such medical books and articles in the country for reference. On the one hand, the time available for writing each day is limited. Collecting materials is time-consuming and energy-consuming. The effort is far greater than translation. Moreover, he did not dare to immediately publish the first draft, but put it aside for revisions for more than a year. This is why the publication was delayed.

The entire book is divided into three volumes. The first volume is on bacterial infectious diseases, with 19 chapters. The second volume is on animal infectious diseases, with 18 chapters. The third volume is on special infectious diseases, which include those caused by filterable viruses and those whose pathogens are not yet known, with 14 chapters. The infectious diseases described in the three volumes total 59 kinds. Part of it has been used as a lecture note of pediatric science in National Shanghai Medical College. Therefore, this book can be used as a textbook and as a reference book for practicing physicians. Moreover, the book also includes many photos, all of which were obtained from clinical practice, which will undoubtedly add a lot of value.

In short, this book carefully classifies and lists all infectious diseases in children. It is particularly precise in the area of diagnosis. It can be called a great work of modern pediatrics. It is said that the book has already been published and is sold by the business department of the Wuzhou Pharmacy on Fourth Avenue in this city.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 192

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Second Chapter: Engaging in Commerce, Entering the Folk, Returning to Yongshou, Saying Goodbye to Family, Arriving in Chang'an, a Celestial Person Reaches Chang'an

Thus, these three women, in order of age, followed behind. Jia Duocai turned his body to the side and turned his head to ask: "Old lady, do you think Chang'an City is good?" The old woman said: "I've never been there." The girl behind said: "Duh! Chang'an is Xi'an, haven't you been there?" The old woman said: "Oh! You mean this place, it's extremely good, if there is a paradise in the human world, this is paradise, right?" Jia Duocai said: "If you say so, you are very willing to live here after arriving here." The old woman said: "How would I know? My relatives' family is also very poor. I look at it that way, I'm afraid they can't afford to support me." When Li Shilian heard these words, he felt that Jia Duocai's words were leading to the point, so he gently touched his arm. He originally didn't seem to care much about these women. Now that the people on the side could see it somewhat clearly, he was embarrassed to say more, so he remained silent for a while and walked along the road. The old woman suddenly thought of something and asked, "Sir, what is your honorable surname?" Jia Duocai smiled and said, "Why call me sir? I am not an official." Li Shilian interrupted and said, "His surname is Jia, he is from the bank. He has more money than an official." The old woman said, "Yin Bank, Mao Bank, aren't you in the military? Ah! Not a sir, a battalion commander, right?" Li Shilian said, "We all live in Little Western Paradise, if you have anything, you can go there to find us." Jia Duocai said, "Old Li, this is you causing trouble." Li Shilian smiled and said, "What's the big deal? We can help them a little." The old woman said, "Ah! We poor people always depend on the light of you gentlemen." (35)

The Originator of Circus Performing 193

— Fu Fan

Last year, the Haijing Circus caused a sensation in the city; the month before last, the Hamston Circus also arrived, and it is said that business was also very prosperous. The general public knows that the so-called circus today originated in the West, but before the West introduced circuses to our country, our country originally had something similar to a circus, but the name was different, and the organization was not as complete.

The content of a circus troupe, in addition to the performers showing off some skills, the biggest feature is teaching animals to act. Sometimes, those who travel around selling medicine in our country also play with bears. Isn't this our country's unique small circus troupe? But teaching ferocious beasts like tigers and leopards to act is rarely seen in our country. Training them to do other kinds of actions existed as early as four or five thousand years ago. Although training ferocious beasts to perform other actions is completely different in nature from circus troupes teaching animals to act, the desire to make fierce and stubborn beasts obey human commands is the same. In the Yellow Emperor's era, the Yan Emperor raised troops and fought with the Yellow Emperor on the plains of Banquan. At that time, the Yellow Emperor trained ferocious beasts to fight. The "Records of the Five Emperors" in the "Records of the Grand Historian" says that he taught bears, luo, pixiu, and tigers to fight with the Yan Emperor on the plains of Banquan, which refers to this. Then, the Yellow Emperor, who taught ferocious beasts to fight according to human will, can be said to be the originator of training ferocious beasts in circus troupes.

Although the scent of face powder is fragrant, it inevitably carries some vulgarity.

Record of Strange Flavors of Luodian (Part 2) 195

— Zhang Huang

Two, Section on Noodles and Pastries

Tight Yeast Steamed Buns: Many people say that the tight yeast steamed buns of Nanxiang are famous, but little do they know that the tight yeast steamed buns of Luodian are far superior in practice! The outer skin of Luodian's tight yeast steamed buns is as thin as a very thin wonton wrapper, and it contains a lot of juice. It's best to eat them hot right out of the steamer. They are usually filled with pork, but now that clams and crabs are in season, they are excellent ingredients for filling steamed buns. Moreover, the crabs in the Qingshui River are also superior products. If you ask the shop to make steamed buns filled with shrimp or chicken, it is also very convenient. Of course, the taste will be better than pork filling. Once you have eaten Luodian's tight yeast steamed buns, you will feel that the products of Nanxiang are like a recluse who steals fame purely through pretense, and as for those made by shops around the City God Temple in Shanghai, they are even [beneath mentioning]!

Loose Yeast Steamed Buns: They are still a kind of steamed bun, but loose yeast steamed buns have their own advantages. Loose yeast steamed buns are huge, about the size of a rice bowl. They are as soft as cotton, which is due to the thorough fermentation. Seeing the shape of freshly steamed loose yeast buns, it is easy to think of the breasts of a woman with healthy beauty! Commonly sold, there are large meat fillings and lard filling, of course, there are also a large amount of capacity, but those who truly appreciate loose yeast buns still love the particularly soft dough. If you prepare your own fine filling and give it to the shop to make to order, it will naturally complement each other and be even more delicious! This kind of palatable and easy-to-satiate pastry has the flavor of northern pasta!

Cut Noodles: Long noodles, cut by hand under a knife on a board, I don't know why, the method of the Luodian noodle maker cuts them particularly thin! This is a fundamental advantage, no matter what kind of toppings are used to make soup noodles or fried noodles, they are always superior and welcomed by those who like to eat noodles and are specially mentioned.

Three, Section on Dry Pastries

Lard Chicken Cake: The dry pastries mentioned here are limited to those sold in shops. The lard chicken cake is one of the most famous. Lard pieces are embedded all over the surface, and the chicken eggs are mixed in the noodles in a particularly large amount, creating a fragrant, sweet, fatty, and soft food. It's best to happen to buy it when it's just made, everyone praises it as the ultimate cake, even the various styles of cakes in Western pastries can't catch up with it; however, most of the time you buy it cold, you should still not be afraid of trouble when you bring it back, steam it first when you want to eat it, and it will be no different from the taste when it was just made. Because the size is very inconsistent, the selling price is based on weight rather than the number of pieces.

Honey Cake: The honey cake produced in Luodian's tea shop is much softer than anywhere else! It also has one advantage: it is not as overly sweet as most other places make it, so you can eat a little more. Westerners call the one-month period of a new marriage the "honeymoon." In our country's old customs, honey cakes were used as gifts in wedding ceremonies, also adopting the meaning of [sweet as honey]. I think if people want to use honey cakes in weddings, they should buy Luodian's honey cakes. Then, the relationship between the couple in the future will be as close and sticky as Luodian's honey cake, like glue and lacquer, difficult to separate, which is interesting!

Three Key Points of the North China Conference 196

Records of Lingering Fragrance 197

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

She stared blankly at this clear, long river for a long time, seeming to be very engrossed in it.

[Ah! This place is really lovely! It's a pity we forgot something!] Although she looked slightly disappointed, her voice was still very soft. [Wouldn't it be fun if we had brought the yacht?]

The Empress Dowager was very fond of boating. She had two yachts prepared for her use. Whenever she was happy, she would row back and forth on Kunming Lake in the Summer Palace. Unfortunately, these two yachts were really too big and clumsy. It took many eunuchs to row them at the same time, so it felt uninteresting. If they were to be loaded, they would at least have to occupy a flatcar. But I can say with certainty that if the Empress Dowager had known before setting off that there was such a lovely long river here that could be enjoyed, she would not have hesitated to specially arrange a flatcar to bring the yacht along. Even if she had not known in advance, and there was now a very quick way to send someone back to load it immediately, she would not have hesitated to send someone to fetch one at any cost. Unfortunately, there is no such good method now. It takes at least two days to go back and forth from here to Beijing. Could we let the Empress Dowager wait here? Therefore, she did not even think of this idea. She just sighed repeatedly, expressing infinite regret and longing. I couldn't help but ask her privately what she would do if we really brought the yacht. This question excited her very much, like a thirsty person who hears someone mention the taste of tea. She said that she wanted to sit in the yacht with us, while the rest of the people would remain in the carriage. But the carriage had to move very slowly, side by side with the yacht. This way of playing was certainly very novel! She could not only fully enjoy the pleasure of boating, but also admire the newly made set of toys! This yellow train! Slowly rolling on the track. However, she did not consider how much effort it would take for so many people to move the boat and carriage together! (145)

Overseas Rare News

Record of the British National Nude Movement Congress 199

— Special Correspondent

The nude movement is now being promoted in many countries. Last month, nude movement enthusiasts from various parts of Britain gathered in London to hold their first national congress. Naturally, they held the meeting in secret, so apart from their comrades and a few press representatives, no one knew the location of the gathering, which was in a huge building surrounded by high walls.

Nude movement participants came from as far away as Scotland, and many came in groups from the north and central regions to attend. The opening ceremony was held in a square. All the male and female members, except for six people, were completely naked, lying down or sitting. First, the chairman and secretary gave speeches, and they were also unclothed. The members included men and women of all ages, from elderly people with wrinkled skin to a four-year-old girl. Among them were lawyers, doctors, teachers, and even a nonconformist minister. There was also one Japanese person and one person with one leg.

While the meeting was in progress, suddenly someone saw a ladder leaning against the roof. It turned out that a photographer was trying to secretly take pictures of the meeting. The crowd was immediately alarmed and shouted wildly, "Destroy his film!" "Get him down quickly!" Later, the ladder was taken away, and the crowd allowed the photographer to watch from a window in a high building.

Chairman Schaller said in his opening remarks: "This is the first national congress of the nude movement in Britain, and it is also the first time we have invited the press to participate. We ask the press to take this movement seriously and not to regard it as a fantasy or a joke. The nude movement is suitable for all kinds of people in society and seeks complete equality between men and women of all nations. We are prepared to thoroughly implement this movement." The members then discussed the practical issues of the movement for a long time. The chairman suddenly asked who had a watch to see what time it was. Everyone looked at each other because they had nothing on their bodies at this time, so where would a watch come from? Later, a non-sunbather reported the time to the crowd.

After the meeting, the male and female members walked around the room naked. In the evening, the members organized various games, and a female physical education instructor gave commands to guide everyone in gymnastics, all still completely naked. On the day the male and female members participated in the meeting, after getting up, it didn’t take long for everyone to finish washing up. The men only tidied up their faces, and the women only combed their hair. Neither wore bathrobes nor trousers. The meeting took place in the sunlight all day long. When eating snacks, a cool breeze blew across the square, and several members showed signs of shivering, obviously unable to withstand the cold.

It cannot be said that the British nude movement has become widespread throughout the country, but according to a London correspondent for the Scottish newspaper, the number of southerners joining this movement is gradually increasing. People in the London business and professional circles now often take their families to sunbathing centers on weekends, wearing very light clothing for outdoor recreation and swimming, but the number of people not wearing clothes seems to be increasing daily.

Judging from the current situation, all groups participating in this movement can strictly observe etiquette, but it is very difficult to persuade ordinary people on the street to join. The only difficulty is that to improve their health, they must be in a place surrounded by high walls and have a membership certificate. There is always an unspeakable mystery about nudism. It is not as good as in the countryside or at the beach, where one can wear a backless swimsuit or other simple clothing, without any restraint, and freely sunbathe or do other exercises. One is less troublesome, and it does not hinder others, but the promoters of the nude movement have a different view.

Economic Supplement

A Review and Outlook on China's Credit Investigation Industry 200

— Pan Wenan

I. The Significance of Credit Investigation

The credit investigation industry is an ancillary activity that arises from credit transactions. According to the analysis of general economists, the methods of human transactions can be divided into three periods: (1) the barter period; (2) the monetary transaction period; and (3) the credit transaction period. Today, we have entered the third period, which is that the commercial activities of people in civilized countries cannot be separated from the relationship of credit. What exactly is the meaning of the word "credit"? This can be explained in two layers:

First, from the perspective of commodity relations: Under the current social system, on the one hand, producers add raw materials and labor to produce finished goods; on the other hand, vendors sell the finished goods produced by producers to consumers. According to the principle of transactions, after the vendor obtains the goods from the producer, they should pay the producer the equivalent amount of money, and the transaction is completed. However, since the emergence of the credit system, the situation is different. When the producer sells the goods to the vendor, the vendor must wait until several days or months later before paying the equivalent amount of money to the producer. Then we have to study why the producer is willing to give the vendor a time concession for the money receivable and bear a considerable risk themselves? This is the role of the credit system.

Second, from the perspective of capital relations: On the one hand, the financial industry receives deposits from the social masses and has a large amount of capital; on the other hand, industry and commerce need considerable capital to operate freely. Therefore, the financial industry must find reliable industries and businesses to fully lend out the income funds in order to seek profit; industry and commerce must seek help from the financial industry to obtain capital assistance in order to expand profits. However, most of the funds lent by financial institutions are received from depositors and are responsible for repayment upon maturity or at any time. Therefore, the highest principle of lending funds is safety. Then, what standards does the financial industry use to determine the degree of safety and select its customers? That is the customer's credit. A good degree of credit is safe, otherwise it is not safe. Therefore, credit is of supreme authority in today's society.

Now that we understand the role of the credit system, we can now further study what the credit investigation industry is all about. Simply put, the credit investigation industry is a kind of credit investigation industry in the sale and purchase of commodities and the supply and demand of funds. In detail, before the producer sells the goods on credit to the vendor, they must first assess the latter's creditworthiness. If the creditworthiness is excellent, the credit transaction can be completed, otherwise it will definitely fail. Similarly, before the financial industry lends funds to industry and commerce, it must first assess the latter's creditworthiness to protect the safety of principal and interest. These two types of credit investigation work are the credit investigation industry. We said earlier that the credit investigation industry is an ancillary activity to credit transactions, and that is also what we mean.

II. Historical Review of the Credit Investigation Industry

The agencies that handle credit investigation can be divided into two types: public and private. Public credit investigation agencies specialize in investigating industrial and commercial credit and market news and providing reports as their business. Anyone who wants to lend money or extend credit can consult them about the creditworthiness of their customers. They are generally called credit bureaus. The United Kingdom was the first to establish one, starting in 1830. Subsequently, other countries established them one after another. The United States started in 1840, France in 1857, Germany in 1860, and Japan in the 25th year of Meiji. Up to now, the achievements of the various countries are remarkable, especially the United States and Japan. The two companies in the United States, R.G. Dun and G.C. Bradrtnet, are world-renowned. Their reports on economic and credit conditions are regarded as the standard throughout the country. The Osaka Commercial Credit Bureau and the Tokyo Credit Bureau in Japan are also very well developed. As for private credit investigation agencies, they are the credit investigation departments established by the banks and commercial firms themselves. Their task is to investigate the economic situation and solvency of customers who request financial credit. This type of credit investigation department is now commonly established in larger commercial firms and banks in Europe, America, and Japan. In countries such as the United Kingdom and the United States, there is another type of organization, which is a periodic gathering of credit investigation or accounting personnel from the same industry to exchange customer credit information. If a certain business or individual defaults on a payment owed to a certain company in the industry, then the attending member of the company will specifically mention the name of the business owing the debt to alert the industry. In this way, those with poor credit or those who intend to default on debts can be warned, which can invisibly play the role of superior wins and inferior loses, and improve the morality of merchants.

China lags behind in everything, industry and commerce are immature, and the credit system has not been fully utilized, so it is naturally difficult to expect the development of the credit investigation industry. As far as the public credit investigation industry is concerned, in May of the tenth year of the Republic of China, the Second Joint Conference of Banking Associations was held in Tianjin. The Shanghai Banking Association proposed the establishment of a credit bureau, and the Tianjin Banking Association proposed the organization of a domestic and foreign business intelligence investigation office. After discussion, it was decided that each region should establish its own first. As for the member level, the location should not be limited. The Tianjin Banking Association notified the various associations based on the resolution, expressing its advocacy. Although this resolution added some points to the history of China's credit investigation industry, the actual work can be said to be still untouched.

The Chinese are fond of watching and waiting when things happen, lacking the spirit of courage to move forward, and the result is always giving foreigners the opportunity to take the lead. The credit investigation industry is certainly no exception. When the Joint Conference of Banking Associations put the resolution to establish a credit bureau on the shelf, the Americans and Japanese were already doing it in Shanghai. In the past 20 years, foreign-funded credit bureaus have numbered as many as the following five:

Business Trust Bureau

Tokyo Credit Bureau Shanghai Branch

Imperial Credit Bureau Shanghai Branch

Shanghai Credit Bureau

It is a joke that the credit of Chinese people living in this country must be investigated by foreigners from other countries, but in this situation of scarcity, general banks and manufacturers are flocking to them to collect credit information!

In terms of private credit investigation agencies, in the past six or seven years, a small number of banks have established credit investigation departments, such as the Bank of China, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Xingye Bank, and Zhejiang Industrial Bank. However, under the concept of focusing on the street-running system, the investigation departments of various banks are just making do with what is available, and are just a decoration. It is probably far from the truth to want to fully发挥 their functions.

The above is the situation before the 23rd year. After the two incidents of the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, on the one hand, because the situation of industry and commerce in Shanghai was getting worse and worse, and the sales of Japanese goods were affected by the boycott and greatly declined, most of the credit bureaus run by Japanese merchants closed down; on the other hand, because the banking industry had a new awareness, it recognized that in order to achieve the sound development of industry, commerce, and finance, it must first seek communication and adjustment between the two parties. Therefore, the China Credit Bureau followed in the footsteps of the Joint Preparatory Committee and was produced, giving the credit investigation industry a bright outlook.

III. Investigation of the Current Situation of the Credit Investigation Industry

The motives of the Shanghai banking industry for establishing a credit bureau can be divided into three points: First, in the past, the credit investigations of various banks, in addition to the information provided by foreign-run credit agencies, also sent their own personnel to investigate and inquire in various ways, based on the most reliable judgment; however, there were often cases where Bank A was investigating a certain commercial firm, and Bank B was also busy inquiring about a certain commercial firm, so the two banks spent a lot of effort, but the result was a duplicate work; now if there is a common agency that concentrates the credit investigation data of the various banks as a whole, when each bank needs to investigate a certain commercial firm, it can first use the existing data as a preliminary reference, and then the agency will conduct a detailed investigation, make a report, and distribute it to the banks that need it, wouldn't it be more effective? Second, after the January 28th Incident, most of the credit bureaus run by the Japanese stopped operating, and the banks lacked sources of information. Third, foreigners' investigations of Chinese credit, at best, only get some superficial knowledge. To know the detailed background, foreigners cannot do it; therefore, even in the past few years, the reports sent by foreigners to the banks have gradually lost their credibility, and they have long had the intention of running their own credit bureaus. With the above three motivations, the China Credit Bureau, run by the Chinese themselves, was produced in June of the 21st year.

The business of the China Credit Bureau is divided into three items: (1) Investigation of credit and business intelligence (2) Directory of Banks and Firms, (3) Debt Collection. Except for the third item, which has not yet been launched, the first two items have been quite effective; domestic and foreign banks and manufacturers have heard the news and joined as members one after another, and even foreign credit investigation agencies have signed contracts with them to exchange information. In addition to establishing a general office in Shanghai, the bureau also has branches and agencies in Hankou and Chongqing. The development of the business can be seen in general.

The establishment of the China Credit Bureau can be regarded as creating a model for China's publicly owed credit agencies, and there is unlimited potential for future development. In terms of private credit investigation agencies, almost all banks in Shanghai have now established special investigation departments or special personnel, striving to contact each other on the exchange of information externally, and striving to integrate with the business internally, each moving forward on the road of supporting the good and eliminating the bad, and distinguishing between surplus and deficit.

IV. Several Prerequisites for Promoting the Credit Investigation Industry

The creation of a new business must have the existence of a congenital environment that nurtures this business, and to achieve long-term progress, it must also have a very suitable situation and give it considerable cultivation. After the January 28th Shanghai War, due to the several reasons mentioned above, the objective conditions for establishing a credit bureau were created, and now the scale is roughly complete. To achieve prosperity and growth, the following prerequisites must also be prepared:

First, social support. Old-fashioned merchants often regard credit bureaus as a kind of detective agency. When they see representatives of credit bureaus, they do not ask right from wrong, and they close their doors and refuse to meet them, avoiding them as if they were a scourge, which has caused great difficulties in terms of collecting information. In all fairness, the purpose of the credit bureau is to give good and excellent people the opportunity to be known to the society as much as possible, and to give the society a warning to be cautious about bad and inferior people; in simple terms, it is to improve business ethics. Since the credit bureau has shouldered this bright purpose and is working hard for the society, then all members of the society naturally have the obligation to be frank and helpful, which goes without saying. Second, system improvement. The reason why the credit investigation industry in Europe, America, and Japan has made rapid progress is of course due to the long history, and the greatest convenience is that the content of the business community is comparatively willing to be public in terms of habits, so that the credit bureau has the opportunity to find out its business figures and accurately determine its surplus and deficit level. We only see that the foreign-owned limited companies have the announcement of the final report after the end of each accounting year. The larger companies must publish the final report in the newspapers; even private enterprises are much more open than in China. Looking back at China's business community, except for banks, there are almost no limited liability organizations that publish their final reports in newspapers, and even single-book business reports are not easily leaked to those who are not closely related. In fact, the essence of a limited liability company should be to publicly disclose its financial status to the outside world, because this can make it convenient for creditors to explore its content and protect their rights and interests. Regarding this point, we hope that the government will urge improvements in the future, so that the credit bureau will not encounter great difficulties in investigating companies.

Moreover, various European and American countries have long implemented income tax and inheritance tax. The properties of groups or individuals are all subject to official investigation, so it is comparatively easy to investigate. However, in China, to investigate a private enterprise or individual, if the enterprise or individual has little association with the outside world, it is extremely difficult to determine the amount of its property; even the lending officers of banks only use a vague estimate of "substantial content" or "average family background" to perfunctorily deal with the customer's background, unlike the credit investigation reports of European and American countries and the credit investigations of banks and commercial firms on their customers, which often have accurate figures listed. It is not difficult to imagine the difficulty in handling affairs and the advantages and disadvantages of the business between these two.

What is the Purpose of Leaving Houses Vacant Rather Than Reducing Rent? 201

— Bingzhong

The issue of rent reduction in this city has been clamoring for years, and it is still in the process of appealing and petitioning; those who are unfortunate have already been involved in court lawsuits and are paying the full amount. In theory, rent is a contractual act, and once it has been agreed upon, there is only one way to pay according to the contract; if there are special circumstances, the civil law does not necessarily prohibit relief, but it is difficult to say whether it can be established. Therefore, if you want to reduce the rent but not pay the rent, even if you deposit the rent into the bank, it is a breach of contract until you get a rent receipt; judicial officials only know how to enforce the law, and once the landlord sues for arrears of rent, the tenant is rarely not defeated. Others also lack the courage to resolve this matter. Not only is it difficult to set a rent reduction rate, but even if a rate can be set, disputes will inevitably be severe.

Because it cannot meet the wishes of both parties, it is inevitable. Therefore, if we talk about reduction, we will offend the wealthy families and affect donations and receipts; if we do not reduce, we are afraid of resentment from the people. [If you are not crazy or deaf, it is difficult to be a father-in-law.] Rather than being in a dilemma, why not remain silent and ignore it?

Then will the rent reduction issue be resolved without doing anything? This is not something I can know. The most natural solution is when there are no people renting new houses, and fewer people living in old houses, and after a long period of time, the landlord will not be able to avoid reducing the rent even if they want to. Now, this phenomenon does not exist. Although there are many vacant houses, the vacant ones are mostly city houses, and fewer are lane houses; those lane houses that are vacant are mostly Western-style or old, and fewer are Chinese-style. Since there is no fear that there will be no one living in the houses, and the newly built houses rent for as much as 70 yuan per month for a single building up and down, and the houses are rented out as soon as they are not completely completed, it can be seen that there is still a great need for houses, and the rent price is not expensive. Is it not ridiculous for landlords to laugh at the mention of rent reduction at this time? Even if we retreat and seek "pigeon cage style" houses? As for the fee for tenants to take over the house, the rent is cheap, but they still demand a huge amount of takeover fees, which has not decreased, and it is enough to help the landlords maintain the arrogance of the original rent and weaken the voice of rent reduction.

Some say that it is better to reduce the rent than to leave it vacant, and if the rent is reduced, someone will rent it, which is better than leaving it vacant without reducing the rent. This reason is indeed a good calculation for us who rely on others to live in houses. But for those who have property, especially those who operate real estate, it is better to leave it vacant than to reduce the rent. Generally, those who have real estate hope to increase the value of their property and increase their wealth, which is the same psychology. And those who operate real estate are even more eager for the value of real estate to increase, and they can't wait to buy it today, raise the price tomorrow, and sell it the day after tomorrow to make huge profits immediately. But how to make real estate prices rise is naturally created by its environment. Dense population, convenient transportation, and prosperous markets will make real estate expensive. If real estate is expensive, then its rent must be high. Conversely, if the rent is low, then the real estate in the area must be cheap. Since the changes in real estate and rent are directly proportional, the increase or decrease in rent affects the increase or decrease in real estate value, because the rent is originally the interest on real estate investment. Therefore, those who purchase ready-made real estate must calculate the rental income, which is approximately the rate of return on investment before purchasing it. Those who build new houses must also calculate the annual interest rate, and then evenly divide it into the rental cost of the houses. Now, if the rent is reduced, it will reduce the profit they should get, which will also reduce the value of their investment amount. For the sake of maintaining the excellent value of their real estate, those with financial resources have to take the path of preferring to have vacant spaces and refusing to reduce the rent, believing that they will not rent it out unless they charge the rent they want. Those with less financial resources or rents that are too high will offer a kind of disguised rent reduction, that is, those who have lived for a full year will be offered one month's rent for free, but the rent amount has never changed. All of this is because they are unwilling to reduce their rental value, because there is a danger of depreciating the value of their property once the rent is reduced, and there is a fear of making a profit or loss in the accounts. Therefore, they would rather leave it vacant and rather pay legal fees than reduce the rent.

I would like to say a word for those who generally demand rent reduction. If you also open your eyes wide, you should know that many houses on the market now are invested by you and entrusted to others to operate. Why? Because the deposits in bank trusts are the money you have saved from your hard work and blood. Banks collect your deposits and do not use them to develop industrial and commercial industries to recover interests and rights, but use them in the real estate industry to make profits. The towering buildings rise high into the clouds, and the branch offices are lined up like cigarette paper grocery stores. Don't envy them, don't be surprised, they are all built from the flesh and bones of the depositors. Then today's unwillingness to reduce the rent, how can we not say that it is for the sake of guaranteeing the stability and solidity of your deposits, why should you advocate rent reduction and invite self-inflicted harm!

Moreover, if the rent is reduced, the house donation will be less, and if the land price falls, the tax revenue will be insufficient. This is a matter of interests beyond the owners. From this point of view, the general issue of rent reduction involves too much and is difficult to resolve. Moreover, Chinese and foreigners are mixed together, and a unified method may not be able to pass without obstruction. I am afraid that years of struggling and procrastinating are also here.

To solve the problem of living, it is not just a simple rent problem. Low rent is certainly welcomed by tenants, but its benefits are not entirely concentrated on the tenants. There are plenty of opportunities for "second landlords" to profit even if the rent is cheap. There are also cases where the rent is too low, and the landlord is unprofitable, allowing it to collapse without repairing it or building anything, causing the market to suffer as a result, as was the case in Zhabei before the January 28th Incident. Generally, the structure of rent is approximately as follows:

(Land price + building sale + equipment cost) X interest rate = interest

Rent + interest + donations and taxes = ?

The high price of rent is promoted by the land valuation being increased each time. High land prices mean high costs, which makes rent expensive. However, the increase in land prices is what both the public and private sectors want. What techniques can be used to limit it? There is no other way but to implement Mr. Sun Yat-sen's method of equalizing land rights, using the excess profits for public use, so that those who manipulate land prices have nothing to covet, and land prices can be returned to a flat standard, and rent can be expected to stabilize. The second is to start organizing housing construction cooperatives, and at the same time finance funds to realize it, but this is not something that can be done by those with small assets, nor can it be done by the general public. Even if funds are financed, the debt will be high when the houses are completed with high interest loans of more than 10%. The other is to hope that more affordable housing will be built for the use of general salaried workers, which is also slim. The current affordable housing is mostly intended for those living in grass huts, and it is not even possible to [leave the dark valley and move to the tall trees,] let alone the rest!

The Trend of Vacant Houses in Shanghai 202

— Yang Dehui

Shanghai's population has surged from 75,000 eighty years ago to 3,360,000 today. In the near future, the trend of population increase is unlikely to stop here, which no one can deny. Because of the population increase, the need for housing will naturally increase! And the demand for land will also increase in value due to the increase in housing construction. Whether a city expands depends on the accurate results of population growth and decline. The relationship between housing construction, population expansion, and rising land prices is inherently linked. In such a situation of constant change in Shanghai, the living conditions are worth understanding. Moreover, the recent rent reduction movement is also based on residential issues!

In Shanghai, the types of housing construction are divided according to needs: warehouses, city houses, apartments, offices, Chinese-style residences, and Western-style residences. Except for warehouses, apartments, and offices, the residential aspects are Chinese and Western-style residences. The status of Shanghai's housing situation in the past 33 years can be accurately assessed from housing rentals. The following table refers to the public concession area, but the public concession area can be seen as a microcosm of the entire Shanghai.

Rented Houses Unrented Houses

Year Chinese Western Year Chinese Western

1902 2.8 3.4 1919 2.2 2.0

1903 2.0 7.0 1920 0.8 2.3

1917 3.1 3.7 1934 5.3 14.0

(Note) The fourth quarter of each year is taken as the standard. 1934 is the first quarter.

In the above table, the vacancy rate for Western-style houses was the lowest in 1901, only 1.4%, and the highest in 1910, at 14.8%. This was because it coincided with the stock market frenzy, resulting in so many vacant houses. Last year, 1933, the vacancy rate reached 12.8%, and in the first quarter of this year, it was 14.0%, setting a high record since 1910. As for Chinese-style residences, the vacancy rate is lower than that of Western-style residences, as clearly indicated in the table. This is because the population in the public concession is mainly Chinese. Over the years, the domestic situation has been unstable, with natural disasters and man-made calamities, and the devastation by communist bandits. Generally, the slightly wealthy class considers the concession to be a safe haven, so they have all come to live in the concession. Because of this, the vacancy rate in the last three years has only accounted for four-sixths, which is 8/6 less than the vacancy rate of Western-style residences! At the same time, it is difficult to find stylish and beautiful Chinese-style residences, so people generally have to rent Western-style residences, which has been increasing year by year. In 1905, the rate of Chinese people living in Western-style residences was 10.3%, 12.3% in 1910, 18.5% in 1915, 21.5% in 1910, 22.2% in 1925, 34.7% in 1930, and it had reached 40.5% in 1932, showing the current trend of Chinese people living in Western-style houses. As mentioned above, the vacancy rate of Chinese-style residences is lower than that of Western-style residences due to the increase in the number of Chinese people in the concession. In 1905, there were 45,328 Chinese-style residences, housing a population of 452,816 people. By 1930, there were 77,907 residences, housing a population of 971,397 people. In the past 25 years, the population has clearly increased by more than half, while the number of residences has not even doubled. Therefore, the overcrowding of residences is inevitable. In Shanghai, an average of six families live in one city house, including the front and back buildings, front and back living rooms, attic, and kitchen. Therefore, living in Shanghai is truly like living in a pigeon coop. Comfort is out of the question, and hygiene is never mentioned. How distressing this is! Although living in pigeon coop-style houses, the price is only affordable for people with middle-class income, so they have to shrink their living space. This is why vacant houses are becoming increasingly common, and many bustling places are also empty. This is not because of a decrease in population, but because the heavy burden of rent has led to austerity measures. I hope that landlords in general would find it more beneficial to reduce rents than to leave houses vacant.
