American Cotton Estimated to Have a Bountiful Harvest

New York, 15th. A report on the cotton market for the week states that the cotton market this week has been quite volatile, as many parties continue to close out positions, and retail investors in the South and speculators are also selling. However, when prices fall, there is some short covering and buying by the industry. The weakness of the wheat market and the fluctuations in the exchange rate are the reasons for the disturbance in the cotton market. Furthermore, private cotton production estimates have raised expectations of a bountiful cotton harvest. It is heard that the underlying prices in the South remain firm, but this news and the report of an increase in the amount of new cotton pledged at 1.2 jiao loans have failed to stimulate buying interest and have only shaken the confidence of the old bulls. In terms of effectiveness, the 1.2 jiao loan currently has the power to maintain market prices. The manager of the Producer's Cooperative Sales Agency claims that, comparatively speaking, the bids obtained by the agency are very few that are acceptable, and there is no need to sell much now. More sales must wait until prices are slightly higher, and holders of licensed cotton can sell more when they hand over their licenses to the agency. At the same time, the cotton market is on a firm footing, and many people believe that the amount of sales will inevitably decrease, as cotton farmers have more support from government loans, and more are holding back from selling cotton than before.

Commentary

Interest 208

— Ruomu

All people should have a sense of interest.

So-called interest, in itself, has good and bad distinctions.

Usually, [interest] and [hobby] cannot be confused. The so-called [hobby] belongs to a kind of entertainment, while [interest] is the human [satisfaction of desire] requirement.

Like [labor]! This is a worthwhile painful thing, but some people are engaged in such heavy work, or even regardless of their own lives, and desperately laboring. It is not right to say that they are particularly able to endure hardship. It is because their expectations for harvest are too exciting and too enthusiastic, so they will unconsciously forget the pain.

Although interest does not appear in every occasion that can adapt to human requirements? At the same time, will it always exist because human desires continue to be latent? This is completely denied by general artists. They think that interest is only something that exists temporarily.

How important is the education of interest to life? This fact, like the French master Millet in his The Angelus, can give us a little hint of understanding this problem. In his room, it is painted like this: the evening clouds are dyed golden, and the bells of Ave Maria are ringing. In the distant jungle, the high towers of the temple rise. And in another corner there are two farmers! They are a couple, 丨 are finishing their day's work and embarking on their way home. At this time, when they heard the bell from afar, they lowered their heads, facing each other, and silently prayed to the God of love. [This is a famous painting full of great meaning. At the same time, it is also full of great truths showing [interest]!

In Contradiction 209

— Er

Living in modern society, one often thinks in a certain way, but ends up doing the opposite. The so-called theory and practice become spear and shield. For example, knowing hypocrisy is wrong, one wants to be honest and without pretense, but this often makes it difficult to survive. So, one is forced to resort to hypocrisy. Is this just an individual's fault? It's not that simple. It's the restriction of a contradictory social life that forces individuals to follow society and live in contradiction.

To be honest, we think that women wearing high heels turns them into mere vases and toys, which is not right. But often, seeing a woman in high heels, the beauty of her curves is especially appealing, and one feels it wouldn't be bad to hold and play with her. Even women themselves often feel that wearing high heels is indeed not good for their health, and it's intended to make them a toy for men. But in the end, they go against what they think, cater to social customs, and have to wear high heels to avoid suffering losses in society. Many women wear high heels without realizing this, but how many female students knowingly commit this offense? In particular, there are many women and men who speak out against women being treated as toys, yet they themselves, or their wives, still wear high heels. Isn't this obvious? Why such a contradiction?

Perhaps many people will say that this is because their understanding and will are not thorough, so they cannot put their theories into practice. This is also a reason, but to consider this the complete solution is problematic.

As mentioned above, it is the restriction of the entire social life that leads to contradiction because of the contradictions inherent within it. Therefore, no matter how strong your will, it will largely be restricted by this fundamental constraint, preventing you from transcending this contradictory life.

Does this mean we should just let it go and live in contradiction? Not necessarily. We believe that the cause lies in the contradiction of the entire social life. Therefore, although relying solely on individual will to oppose it has little effect, one must consider this entire contradiction. So, to put it bluntly, the fact that most people live contradictory lives requires a joint effort to fundamentally resolve the contradictions of the entire social life, in order to completely eliminate being trapped in contradiction.

Especially the petit bourgeoisie, are full of contradictions. They understand that the class that dominates society is contradictory, but they often have to rely on it to survive, making it difficult to break away completely and go to the opposite, hostile side of this dominant force to eliminate the contradictions of the rulers. Therefore, they often hover in the middle, living a contradictory life.

If one cannot break away from the entire contradictory social life, even if one's individual will is strong, trying to eliminate the contradiction within oneself will likely be in vain. Only by fundamentally breaking away from the original contradictory life, climbing towards a new direction, and waiting until the contradictions of the entire social life are eliminated, can people generally escape living in contradiction!

There are Exceptions 210

— Ben

Some say that this year marks the end of the intellectual class, and the reality is indeed very serious. First, there was the job-seeking movement of graduates from various universities in Peiping, followed by the response from graduates of National Central University in Nanjing and Great China University in Shanghai, causing a huge commotion. This has sparked comments from all sides, with some saying it is due to the flaws of the absolute social system, and others saying the graduates themselves are unsound and have excessively high desires. Both arguments naturally have their reasons, especially the former being more powerful, without a doubt. However, there are exceptions.

This past Wednesday, a friend, Mr. X, specifically came to see me to ask me to find an agriculture teacher for him. He said he had been looking for a whole week and hadn't found one, knowing that I had some connections with XX Agricultural School, so he came to me for help. I agreed to help him find one, as I knew several friends in that field and had some connections with XX Agricultural School, so I was confident that I could find someone. But the reality turned out to be quite different. It has been a full four days now, and I still haven't found a solution, so I have to tell him to seek help from someone more capable.

Secondly, I personally heard someone mention that graduates of various universities feel they have no way out, but there are exceptions in two schools. One is XX National University in this city, where graduates of a certain banking department were all reserved by banks, and they even asked the school authorities if there were any more. The other is XX National University in Peiping, where graduates of a certain economics department were also all reserved, and they had jobs as soon as they left school, without even the word "unemployment" being mentioned, let alone time to rest.

These are absolute facts, one that I experienced myself, and one that others experienced. From these facts, it can be clearly seen that young people are not completely without a way out, but they themselves must be quite sound. Young people from general "wild chicken" schools will naturally have to frown. Secondly, the Chinese education system does indeed need some reorganization. The prosperity of liberal arts and the crowding of friends who wield pens naturally pose a problem for finding a way out. We are an agricultural country and urgently need to catch up with the industrial process. In fact, we desperately need such talents.

It's Dinner Time! 211

— Baili

Waning Autumn 212

— Xi Zhen

It hasn't been long since the Mid-Autumn Festival. In the village, on the streets, a sparse drizzle falls; the weather turns

Page 20

sultry again. The villagers all sigh idly, looking at the withered rice stalks in the fields. Children over the age of six take small iron shovels at night to steal sweet potatoes from the gardens of wealthy households, bringing them back to make tomorrow's meal. Adults make bamboo baskets and spin cotton thread at home, preparing to sell them on the streets for a few coins to survive the winter. Those with acquaintances in the city run around the streets all day, saying, "You always say you're better off than us. There's famine in the countryside, but surely things aren't that bad in the city. Please help us out."

"Don't say that. City people have their own hardships. You can imagine what the situation is like at this time of year. No one is doing well."

Everyone frowns; there's nothing they can do!

The rain falls unintentionally, and people have no urgent hope at all. It's already August; what hope is there in rain? "Heaven is forcing people to become robbers; there's nothing we can do!"

After a desolate Mid-Autumn Festival (this year, the only incense and candle shop in the town sold only two incense holders in this village of over two hundred households. One was from Master Wang's house at the head of the village, and the other was from the school of Teacher Li), the market after the festival became even more desolate. Five shops in the town closed, one of which was a rice shop: rice rose to eleven yuan and eight jiao, and even middle-class families stopped eating rice. During the three months of drought, only eight shi of rice were sold. Another was the "Jing Guang Sundries" shop owned by Third Uncle's elder brother, Second Son, which started with eighty yuan of capital. People gradually can't even afford sweet potatoes. Some go to the Southern Goods store to buy pearl rice, and others eat rice bran used to feed chickens by wealthy families (which is hard to get; many people wait to grab it every day).

Second Son's family went to Shanghai to work (naturally, they secretly took some of the shop's goods with them). Third Uncle wanted to call A-Hu to go with them, but Second Son and his family refused, saying repeatedly, "We're family, can't you even do this for us? This child can do something. He definitely won't be a burden to you in Shanghai. Let him pull a rickshaw or be a beggar."

Seeing this, A-Hu also left.

Leaving Third Uncle alone, eating four sweet potatoes a day, cursing heaven, cursing the times, cursing fate, cursing the age of fifty-nine, cursing this and that.

That day was the nineteenth. The moon was still very good at dusk, and it was cold enough. The wind brought a bit of a sharp taste. (However, during the day, some people still took their tattered cotton-padded coats and trousers to the pawnshop to ask for three or four hundred coins.) When it got dark, Third Uncle had just gone to bed (at this time of year, no one lit lamps). Shen Fu from Master Wang's house knocked on the door urgently: "Third Uncle, the master wants you to come over."

Trembling, "Brother Shen Fu, come inside and sit. Is it about the field this year? The master went to the countryside to check the rent the other day and saw everything. The famine isn't our fault..."

"No, our whole family is moving to our aunt's house in Shanghai tomorrow. We're so busy tonight that everyone is dizzy. He wants you to come immediately to help move things, and also—"

Also, Master Wang, because Third Uncle was an "old tenant of three generations" and also a single man, clean and tidy, wanted him to watch the empty house.

Under the dim yellow light of the large safe lamp, weary faces were revealed, the master, the mistress, the concubine, and the young master who wore foreign clothes and studied at a university in Shanghai. Everyone had a heart filled with escape. "Get things done early, and leave early tomorrow morning."

Looking at this situation, Third Uncle's heart felt like it was sinking into an ice cave. Such a large family was saying that one day it would collapse. Like attending a funeral, countless indescribable hands were grabbing at his heart.

At night, the moon was good, and Third Uncle slept in Shen Fu's room. "The countryside is finally finished," Shen Fu told him. The eldest young master had asked someone in Shanghai to find him a teaching job, with more than twenty yuan a month. The master still had a hundred or so silver dollars on hand. They said that they would always find a way to survive in Shanghai, at least for a year. "If not, they could even buy lottery tickets."

Shen Fu climbed into bed, turned over, and began to snore. Third Uncle couldn't sleep, his eyes open, watching the moonlight on the ground. There were too many questions contained in his mind. But suddenly, as if he had received some revelation, he thought, "The countryside is definitely finished, but going to Shanghai is at most buying lottery tickets."

With that, he turned over and thought of A-Hu, wandering in the big city.

The night was deathly silent.

Autumn Night 213

— Tu

The autumn wind gently caresses the locust trees by the shore, the leaves whispering softly. The autumn night moon appears especially clear and bright. Although the night is already deep, Yong and I are still wandering by the shore.

The midnight tide is gradually swelling. The waves strike the rocks on the shore, sending up dazzling sprays, emitting a tantalizing sound. Moonlight illuminates the sea, shimmering with silver ripples. The distant, bobbing fishing boats, with their isolated lamps, look like the flickering of will-o'-the-wisps. The seaside of the South is beautiful after all! Especially in this late autumn night.

Silence, silence, all the scenery is silent under the moonlight. Only the sound of the tide and leaves play the nocturne of autumn sorrow in rhythm.

"Ming, look, how beautiful the moon is tonight!"

Yong, who had been silent for a long time, finally opened his kind smile, pointing to the moon that had already hung high in the sky. Unconsciously, a happy smile appeared on his face. He seemed to have forgotten the tangles in his heart. He stood up and took my hand.

"What for? You're so excited?"

"What are you dazing about? Only tonight, let's talk excitedly!"

With just one sentence, I fell silent again. Although there were many words I wanted to say in my heart, they were all stuck in my throat. His excitement made me even more silent.

The autumn night breeze blew into my thin underwear, and I felt a chill. But we were still wandering by the shore, as if the slight autumn wind was blowing into my lonely heart like strands of sorrow. Lowering my head, I looked at our two thin, long shadows, feeling only the sadness of life's journey, like these shadows being trampled by people's feet.

"Ming, don't dream anymore. Tomorrow, I have to leave this place. You know, my family environment won't allow me to stay any longer. A happy life, I'm afraid, won't exist for me anymore. However, I think this departure, one day, we will meet again."

"I also think so, we will meet again."

Moonlight shone on Yong's thin, yellow, pale face. The wind stirred his disheveled hair. The smile that had been so excited on his face gradually faded. His pair of beautiful black eyes stared unblinking at the boundless distance of the sea, silently contemplating.

Night, autumn night, sorrows endlessly as long as silkworm threads, entangling my deep heart. Yong and I finally wandered the entire night by this sea, staggering.

The morning can make people excited. The autumn sun can make people love. On this very morning, Yong, holding a desolate heart, left his old hometown, embarked on a journey, and drifted toward the equator across the vast sea.

A year goes by easily, and it's autumn again. After a year, I finally received news about Yong, and it was unfortunate news! He, my dear friend Yong, lost consciousness three months after arriving on the other side and departed from the world forever.

A young man, a promising young man, finally lost his life in the barrel of the sub-society, under the whip of life.

Autumn, what a sorrowful autumn! Whenever the moon shines in front of the window in the deep night, I can only look at the clear moon, the azure sky, and deeply recall those sorrowful past events.

One of the Curse of Autumn 1934 214

— Xiaolin

People all say that Shanghai is heaven on earth, with gold and silver everywhere. Therefore, Shanghai is worth praising and visiting. If you don't believe it, look at the skyscrapers that reach into the clouds, increasing and being built day by day, and the countless dance halls and taverns that continue to appear. With these money-burning places, isn't Shanghai a world of gold?

Is Shanghai really worth praising? Yet most people are praising it. So from inland cities and villages, hundreds and thousands of people leave their homes and cross mountains and seas to rush to this paradise of Shanghai every day. They bring with them a joyful heart, hoping to pick up gold. As for whether it is easier to find food in Shanghai, that is true. If it's a big place, with so many factories, it shouldn't be difficult to find a bite to eat. But there is more than just one or two people looking for food to eat. Instead, there are countless people opening their mouths and waiting.

Few actually find food to eat. The joy and beautiful hope that filled their hearts before arriving in Shanghai are immediately shattered as soon as they set foot on this land.

Is Shanghai worthy of praise? You have to live there to know. And after living there for a while, you're sure to ask what is there to praise in Shanghai, and instead curse it. But cursing is futile. The stomach cannot be empty all the time; you need to eat. But food is not easily obtained. Having already arrived, there is no work to do, and there is no way to go back. So they become vagrants. Vagrancy, or even turning to crime, makes the world uneasy day by day.

Yes, on the other hand, Shanghai is worthy of praise, with songs, strings, and music, a drunken paradise of gold. But this is, after all, another world, one that has nothing to do with them. Their world is darkness, hunger, disease, and death. So Shanghai is to be cursed. Who says no?

Arrived in Tokyo 215

— Wang Ci

After arriving in Tokyo, I once sent you a postcard. I left Shanghai on the Shanghai Maru at 9:00 AM on June 19th and arrived in Tokyo at 7:20 AM on the 22nd. During these three days and three nights, because I was seasick for two days and two nights and didn't sleep a wink on the train, my body was as exhausted as if I had just recovered from a serious illness, and I couldn't move.

On this trip to Japan, I was accompanied by two classmates named Tang, and we are now living together in the Chinese Dormitory at No. 31, Oiwake-cho, Hongo-ku, Tokyo.

Japanese cuisine is indeed something we cannot eat; and Japanese-style Chinese food (so-called "China cuisine") is also very difficult to swallow.

Although I have arrived in Japan, I don't speak much Japanese, and I often end up tongue-tied and at a loss when dealing with maids. I have now entered the Tokyo Japanese Language School and rush to school, which is six or seven li away, at 8:00 AM every day for classes. For the sake of money, we don't take the train (in Tokyo, there are so many trains that the tracks on the ground are as dense as a spider web, and there are also buses and underground trains, and they are now rushing to build underground train tracks; these underground trains and trains are said to be for the purpose of preventing World War). Therefore, we have a mandatory course of walking eighty minutes every day.

In Japan, the relationship between men and women is nonchalant. On the second night after I first arrived in Japan, a friend named Zhang, who had been living in Japan for more than a year, took me to a Japanese bathhouse. It really surprised me; the Japanese male and female bathhouses are placed in the same room, and their boundary is only a short wall as high as the body. If I were half a head taller, standing at the base of the wall, I could see the movements on the other side. At one end of the short wall, there is a high counter and a small wooden door. Sitting at the counter are young, well-dressed female shopkeepers, and young maids are running back and forth to take care of the dozens of naked men without any hesitation or familiarity. They don't seem to feel any surprise about naked men, because I saw them facing naked men without the slightest shyness. The small door is half-closed, and the maids run back and forth through this door, taking care of both sides. Through the crack in this door, we can see the girls who have finished bathing putting on their pants or tying the small bundles on their backs. The wall is too low, and the sound of water and the sweet voices in the women's bathhouse can be heard very clearly in our ears.

Yesterday, the Tang brothers and I went to [Ueno Park]. In the park, there is a large Western-style building that is the venue for the National Defense Exposition. In front of the entrance to the exposition, there is a large archway that was recently built to commemorate the birth of the Japanese Crown Prince. On this archway, the plaque of [The First Pass Under Heaven] from Shanhaiguan in our country is prominently displayed! Opposite this archway, there is a stone monument commemorating the soldiers who died in the Taiwan Expedition. Around this stone monument, there are Chinese cannons obtained in this battle. (These cannons are erected on the ground and are two and a half feet high. Iron rings are installed on both sides of the cannonballs and connected with iron chains, acting as the iron railings for this stone monument.) To the left of this stone monument, a large iron anchor obtained in this battle is erected there, with a height one and a half times my own. After leaving Ueno Park, the three of us spent 45 sen (worth a little less than 4 jiao 5 fen in Chinese currency) to visit the zoo: this zoo is very grand, as big as twenty animal parks in Shanghai Confucian Temple Park.

Japanese literature books are unexpectedly cheap: a 38-volume [World Literature Collection] in a one-inch-thick, cloth-bound hardcover edition only sells for 10 yen. You have read Japanese, so if you want to buy it, I can buy it for you. I have already written quite a bit. Goodbye! I hope you will write to me often.

A Small Memory 216

— Lie

There was a time when I loved to eat peanuts, almost every day, and I ate a lot of them. So much so that sometimes when I had guests, I considered peanuts to be the best delicacy. Although my friends didn't reject them, most of them showed some strangeness, looking somewhat inexplicable.

But this was my habit three years ago; it's a thing of the past. Now, when I see peanuts, I can't help but feel a bitter taste in my mouth. Speaking of this, I can't help but feel slightly sentimental. First, the short three years of my life have made me less interested in things. Rolling around in society, not only has the habit of eating peanuts disappeared, but many other loves have also been cut off one after another. Now, the only thing I still love is smoking. This is because I am too burdened by life, and I am busy all day long, so I naturally have no leisure. This is something we young people often lament! Secondly, because this habit of eating peanuts has faded, I feel even more lonely in life. This is not just a simple matter of taste.

Speaking of it, the habit of eating peanuts was not inevitable, but accidental. In my hometown, even later when I was studying in the city of C Province, I had never seen peanuts. All there were were groundnuts, and I got a headache just looking at them, let alone eating them.

After I came to Shanghai, during a certain summer, I started eating peanuts. After a period of time, I grew to love them more and more, and so it became my only habit at the time.

My roommate, seeing the sudden growth of this habit, always showed a surprised expression to me. No, he once asserted that [my habit was infected by someone else]. Although I politely explained that it wasn't, he still didn't quite believe it, so I let him laugh.

Speaking of this, there was indeed such an incident. C, a classmate, because of various coincidences, had always shown goodwill to me. But speaking of it, it was just goodwill, nothing else. Even going for a walk outside the school with her or going to the cinema to see a movie would cause people to gossip and be uneasy all day long. It was an environment where jealousy was at its worst. Coincidentally, she also loved to eat peanuts. Although she didn't eat as much as I did, she probably loved them even more.

One day, there was a sudden change, and everyone scattered. It has been several years since I heard any news about her. Yesterday, Mr. W suddenly mentioned her, saying that she had not only become someone's wife, but also a mother. And after these years of social hardship, I no longer have the habit of eating peanuts, which does make people feel…

Storytelling to Music 221

Zhong Xi (1040)

Yao Xiao'an, Pang Xueqing, Pearl Pagoda, 10:45 AM to 11:15 AM, Part Two

Opening Chapter [Fan Zhongyan's Tea Visit] 222

Lifelong upright and honest. Song Dynasty famous minister Fan Zhongyan. Newly appointed Kaifeng as governor. He secretly visits the people in disguise. Who can recognize him as a disguised traveler? He strolls leisurely into the tea house. Holding fragrant tea. Pouring clear spring water. Suddenly sees the master and servant walking in. The tea shop owner greets them bowing, calling them members of the gentry repeatedly. They disagree in several words and act impolitely. Before leaving, they utter malicious words. Upon detailed inquiry, it is learned that Zhang Min is evil. His illegal and overbearing ways are all due to his wealth and power. His family servant helps him in his wickedness, named Zhang Qian. Let's talk about Zhou Yu's case in the past. He loved beauty and cheated people, taking lives. He filled twenty ingots of silver with two ingots. He harmed the scholar and exiled him. At the separation from the court, tears streamed down. Wife separated from children for more than ten years. After investigating and clarifying the evil deeds, he returns to the yamen. He immediately judges with the vermilion brush in the court. Zhang Min's crime is too serious to be forgiven. He hangs a high mirror that reflects without bias. The people admire and praise him again and again.

Opening Chapter: Sister Flowers

The women of Spring River are the most open-minded, they are willing to put in effort with their glamorous attire, powdery white and rouge red, sister flowers, three parts true color and seven parts effort. They are regular patrons of dance halls and cinemas, social flowers emerge from Shanghai East. One is a middle-aged woman, still charming, still worthy of attracting butterflies and bees. One is in her youthful years, naturally charming, not losing the same paired branch flavor, a pair of delicate figures, both healthy and beautiful, slender figures with delicate voices. The new style of hair is permed in spirals, with snow-white skin and jade-like complexion. Willow-leaf eyebrows are pleasing to everyone, cherry-like mouths are dyed crimson. Before the slight cold has passed, they expose their arms first, and as early summer arrives, they bare their chests early. One loves to wear apple green, and one likes to often wear light and dark red. Gauzy silk, hides the double peaks, light steps are wonderfully infinite, round and snowy legs are naturally beautiful, leather shoes with镂花 are like a smooth road. One is that in the Yi Garden, she encounters a young man, a strange fate met on the road, with pledges of love and oaths of eternal alliance, sweet and loving, two hearts as one. One is a chance encounter with a young master from the countryside, seeing him is very fulfilled, feigning affection and diligently offering love, playing with the soul of the villager in the palm of her hand, temporarily borrowing a room to make good times, a thousand gold for a moment in the melting moonlight, completely unaware that form is emptiness and emptiness is form, this body is simply being a moth drawn to a flame, body and soul ruined by desire, extreme joy leads to sorrow and sending off the end, unexpectedly advancing towards the city of unjust death.
